</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Royce, Josiah</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Josiah_Royce" title="Josiah Royce">Josiah Royce</a></span></span></td>
<td>1855–1916</td>
<td>colleague of James at Harvard who employed pragmatism in an idealist metaphysical framework, he was particularly interested in the philosophy of religion and community; his work is often associated with <a href="/wiki/Neo-Hegelianism" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Hegelianism">neo-Hegelianism</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Santayana, George</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/George_Santayana" title="George Santayana">George Santayana</a></span></span></td>
<td>1863–1952</td>
<td>although he eschewed the label "pragmatism" and called it a "heresy", several critics argue that he applied pragmatist methodologies to <a href="/wiki/Naturalism_(philosophy)" title="Naturalism (philosophy)">naturalism</a>, especially in his early masterwork, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Life_of_Reason" title="The Life of Reason">The Life of Reason</a></i>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Du Bois, W. E. B.</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/W._E._B._Du_Bois" title="W. E. B. Du Bois">W. E. B. Du Bois</a></span></span></td>
<td>1868–1963</td>
<td>student of James at Harvard who applied pragmatist principles to his sociological work, especially in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Philadelphia_Negro" title="The Philadelphia Negro">The Philadelphia Negro</a></i> and <i>Atlanta University Studies</i>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Fringe figures</b></p>
<table class="sortable wikitable">
<tr>
<th width="10%">Name</th>
<th width="8%">Lifetime</th>
<th class="unsortable" width="78%">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr valign="top">
<td><span class="sortkey">Papini, Giovanni</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Papini" title="Giovanni Papini">Giovanni Papini</a></span></span></td>
<td>1881–1956</td>
<td>Italian essayist, mostly known because James occasionally mentioned him.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Vailati, Giovanni</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Vailati" title="Giovanni Vailati">Giovanni Vailati</a></span></span></td>
<td>1863–1909</td>
<td>Italian analytic and pragmatist philosopher.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Shi, Hu</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Hu_Shi" class="mw-redirect" title="Hu Shi">Hu Shi</a></span></span></td>
<td>1891–1962</td>
<td>Chinese intellectual and reformer, student and translator of Dewey's and advocate of pragmatism in China.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Niebuhr, Reinhold</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Reinhold_Niebuhr" title="Reinhold Niebuhr">Reinhold Niebuhr</a></span></span></td>
<td>1892–1971</td>
<td>American Philosopher and Theologian, inserted Pragmatism into his theory of Christian Realism.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Neoclassical_pragmatists_.281950.E2.80.93present.29">Neoclassical pragmatists (1950–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pragmatism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Neoclassical pragmatists (1950–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Neoclassical pragmatists stay closer to the project of the classical pragmatists than neopragmatists do.</p>
<table class="sortable wikitable">
<tr>
<th width="10%">Name</th>
<th width="8%">Lifetime</th>
<th class="unsortable" width="78%">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr valign="top">
<td><span class="sortkey">Hook, Sidney</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Sidney_Hook" title="Sidney Hook">Sidney Hook</a></span></span></td>
<td>1902–1989</td>
<td>a prominent New York intellectual and philosopher, a student of Dewey at Columbia.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Levi, Isaac</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Isaac_Levi" title="Isaac Levi">Isaac Levi</a></span></span></td>
<td>1930–</td>
<td>seeks to apply pragmatist thinking in a decision-theoretic perspective.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Haack, Susan</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Susan_Haack" title="Susan Haack">Susan Haack</a></span></span></td>
<td>1945–</td>
<td>teaches at the University of Miami, sometimes called the intellectual granddaughter of C.S. Peirce, known chiefly for <a href="/wiki/Foundherentism" title="Foundherentism">foundherentism</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Rescher, Nicholas</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Rescher" title="Nicholas Rescher">Nicholas Rescher</a></span></span></td>
<td>1928–</td>
<td>advocates a methodological pragmatism that sees functional efficacy as evidentiating validity.</td>
</tr>
</table>
</td>
<td style="text-align: left; vertical-align: top; padding-left: 3em;">
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Analytical.2C_neo-_and_other_pragmatists_.281950.E2.80.93present.29">Analytical, neo- and other pragmatists (1950–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pragmatism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Analytical, neo- and other pragmatists (1950–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>(Often labelled neopragmatism as well.)</p>
<table class="sortable wikitable">
<tr>
<th width="10%">Name</th>
<th width="8%">Lifetime</th>
<th class="unsortable" width="78%">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr valign="top">
<td><span class="sortkey">Bernstein, Richard J.</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Richard_J._Bernstein" title="Richard J. Bernstein">Richard J. Bernstein</a></span></span></td>
<td>1932–</td>
<td>Author of <i>Beyond Objectivism and Relativism: Science, Hermeneutics, and Praxis</i>, <i>The New Constellation: The Ethical-Political Horizons of Modernity/Postmodernity</i>, <i>The Pragmatic Turn</i></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Burke, F. Thomas</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/w/index.php?title=F._Thomas_Burke&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="F. Thomas Burke (page does not exist)">F. Thomas Burke</a></span></span></td>
<td>1950–</td>
<td>Author of <i>What Pragmatism Was</i> (2013), <i>Dewey's New Logic</i> (1994). His work interprets contemporary philosophy of mind, philosophy of language, and philosophical logic through the lens of classical American pragmatism.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Fine, Arthur</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Fine" title="Arthur Fine">Arthur Fine</a></span></span></td>
<td>1937–</td>
<td>Philosopher of Science who proposed the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Ontological_Attitude" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural Ontological Attitude">Natural Ontological Attitude</a> to the debate of <a href="/wiki/Scientific_realism" title="Scientific realism">scientific realism</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Fish, Stanley</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Stanley_Fish" title="Stanley Fish">Stanley Fish</a></span></span></td>
<td>1938–</td>
<td>Literary and Legal Studies pragmatist. Criticizes Rorty's and Posner's legal theories as "almost pragmatism"<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> and authored the afterword in the collection <i>The Revival of Pragmatism</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Hawthorne, John</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/John_Hawthorne" title="John Hawthorne">John Hawthorne</a></span></span></td>
<td></td>
<td>Defends a pragmatist form of <a href="/wiki/Contextualism" title="Contextualism">contextualism</a> to deal with the <a href="/wiki/Lottery_paradox" title="Lottery paradox">lottery paradox</a> in his <i>Knowledge and Lotteries</i>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Lewis, Clarence Irving</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Clarence_Irving_Lewis" title="Clarence Irving Lewis">Clarence Irving Lewis</a></span></span></td>
<td>1883–1964</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Margolis, Joseph</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Margolis" title="Joseph Margolis">Joseph Margolis</a></span></span></td>
<td>1924–</td>
<td>still proudly defends the original Pragmatists and sees his recent work on Cultural Realism as extending and deepening their insights, especially the contribution of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sanders_Peirce" title="Charles Sanders Peirce">Peirce</a> and Dewey, in the context of a rapprochement with Continental philosophy.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Putnam, Hilary</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Hilary_Putnam" title="Hilary Putnam">Hilary Putnam</a></span></span></td>
<td>1926-2016</td>
<td>in many ways the opposite of Rorty and thinks classical pragmatism was too permissive a theory.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Rorty, Richard</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Richard_Rorty" title="Richard Rorty">Richard Rorty</a></span></span></td>
<td>1931–2007</td>
<td>famous author of <i><a href="/wiki/Philosophy_and_the_Mirror_of_Nature" title="Philosophy and the Mirror of Nature">Philosophy and the Mirror of Nature</a></i>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Quine, Willard van Orman</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Willard_van_Orman_Quine" class="mw-redirect" title="Willard van Orman Quine">Willard van Orman Quine</a></span></span></td>
<td>1908–2000</td>
<td>pragmatist philosopher, concerned with <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_language" title="Philosophy of language">language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Logic" title="Logic">logic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Philosophy_of_mathematics" title="Philosophy of mathematics">philosophy of mathematics</a>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Unger, Roberto</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Roberto_Unger" class="mw-redirect" title="Roberto Unger">Roberto Unger</a></span></span></td>
<td>1947–</td>
<td>in <i>The Self Awakened: Pragmatism Unbound</i>, advocates for a "radical pragmatism," one that 'de-naturalizes' society and culture, and thus insists that we can "transform the character of our relation to social and cultural worlds we inhabit rather than just to change, little by little, the content of the arrangements and beliefs that comprise them."</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Sandbothe, Mike</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Mike_Sandbothe" title="Mike Sandbothe">Mike Sandbothe</a></span></span></td>
<td>1961–</td>
<td>Applied Rorty's neopragmatism to media studies and developed a new branch that he called Media Philosophy. Together with authors such as Juergen Habermas, Hans Joas, Sami Pihlstroem, Mats Bergmann, Michael Esfeld, and Helmut Pape, he belongs to a group of European Pragmatists who make use of Peirce, James, Dewey, Rorty, Brandom, Putnam, and other representatives of American pragmatism in continental philosophy.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Shusterman, Richard</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Richard_Shusterman" title="Richard Shusterman">Richard Shusterman</a></span></span></td>
<td></td>
<td>philosopher of art.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Stanley, Jason</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Jason_Stanley" title="Jason Stanley">Jason Stanley</a></span></span></td>
<td>1969–</td>
<td>Defends a pragmatist form of contextualism against semantic varieties of contextualism in his <i>Knowledge and Practical Interest</i>.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Talisse, Robert B.</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Robert_B._Talisse" title="Robert B. Talisse">Robert B. Talisse</a></span></span></td>
<td>1970–</td>
<td>defends an epistemological conception of democratic politics that is explicitly opposed to <a href="/wiki/John_Dewey" title="John Dewey">Deweyan democracy</a> and yet rooted in a conception of <a href="/wiki/Social_epistemology" title="Social epistemology">social epistemology</a> that derives from the pragmatism of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Sanders_Peirce" title="Charles Sanders Peirce">Charles Peirce</a>. His work in <a href="/wiki/Argumentation_theory" title="Argumentation theory">argumentation theory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Informal_logic" title="Informal logic">informal logic</a> also demonstrates pragmatist leanings.</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Toulmin, Stephen</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Stephen_Toulmin" title="Stephen Toulmin">Stephen Toulmin</a></span></span></td>
<td>1922–2009</td>
<td>student of Wittgenstein, known especially for his <i>The Uses of Argument</i>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_pragmatists">Other pragmatists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pragmatism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Other pragmatists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_pragmatists">Legal pragmatists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pragmatism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Legal pragmatists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<td>1841–1935</td>

<td>Judge on <a href="/wiki/U.S._Court_of_Appeals_for_the_Seventh_Circuit" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit">U.S. Court of Appeals for the Seventh Circuit</a>.</td>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Pragmatists_in_the_extended_sense">Pragmatists in the extended sense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pragmatism&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Pragmatists in the extended sense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<td>thinker on race, politics, and religion; operates under the sign of "prophetic pragmatism".</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td><span class="sortkey">Sellars, Wilfrid</span><span class="vcard"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/Wilfrid_Sellars" title="Wilfrid Sellars">Wilfrid Sellars</a></span></span></td>

New Jersey: Pearson. pp.&#160;76,100. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-0-13-285238-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-0-13-285238-8">978-0-13-285238-8</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APragmatism&amp;rft.aufirst=Gerald&amp;rft.aulast=Gutek&amp;rft.btitle=Philosophical%2C+Ideological%2C+and+Theoretical+Perspectives+On+Education&amp;rft.date=2014&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-13-285238-8&amp;rft.pages=76%2C100&amp;rft.place=New+Jersey&amp;rft.pub=Pearson&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-HaackLane2006-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-HaackLane2006_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Susan_Haack" title="Susan Haack">Susan Haack</a>; Robert Edwin Lane (11 April 2006). <i>Pragmatism, old &amp; new: selected writings</i>. Prometheus Books. pp.&#160;18–67. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-59102-359-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-59102-359-3">978-1-59102-359-3</a>.</cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APragmatism&amp;rft.au=Robert+Edwin+Lane&amp;rft.au=Susan+Haack&amp;rft.btitle=Pragmatism%2C+old+%26+new%3A+selected+writings&amp;rft.date=2006-04-11&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-59102-359-3&amp;rft.pages=18-67&amp;rft.pub=Prometheus+Books&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook" class="Z3988"><span style="display:none;">&#160;</span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-BiestaBurbules-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-BiestaBurbules_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-BiestaBurbules_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Biesta, G.J.J. &amp; Burbules, N. (2003). <i>Pragmatism and educational research</i>. Lanham, MD: Rowman and Littlefield.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">James, William (1898), "Philosophical Conceptions and Practical Results", delivered before the Philosophical Union of the University of California at Berkeley, August 26, 1898, and first printed in the <i>University Chronicle</i> 1, September 1898, pp. 287–310. <i>Internet Archive</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/philosophicalcon00jameuoft#page/n4/mode/1up">Eprint</a>. On <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/philosophicalcon00jameuoft#page/290/mode/1up">p. 290</a>:</span>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">I refer to Mr. Charles S. Peirce, with whose very existence as a philosopher I dare say many of you are unacquainted. He is one of the most original of contemporary thinkers; and the principle of practicalism or pragmatism, as he called it, when I first heard him enunciate it at Cambridge in the early [1870s] is the clue or compass by following which I find myself more and more confirmed in believing we may keep our feet upon the proper trail.</span></p>
</blockquote>
<p><span class="reference-text">James credited Peirce again in 1906 lectures published in 1907 as <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Pragmatism:_A_New_Name_for_Some_Old_Ways_of_Thinking" class="extiw" title="s:Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking">Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking</a></i>, see Lecture 2, fourth paragraph.</span></p>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See James (1897), <i>Will to Believe</i> (which James dedicated to Peirce), see p. 124 and footnote via <i>Google Books</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=wRMXL4uYEegC&amp;pg=PA124">Eprint</a>:</span>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">Indeed, it may be said that if two apparently different definitions of the reality before us should have identical consequences, those two definitions would really be identical definitions, made delusively to appear different merely by the different verbiage in which they are expressed.¹<br />
¹ See the admirably original "Illustrations of the Logic of Science," by C. S. Peirce, especially the second paper, "How to make our Thoughts clear,"  [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] in the Popular Science Monthly for January, 1878.</span></p>
</blockquote>
<span class="reference-text">See also James's 1907 <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Pragmatism:_A_New_Name_for_Some_Old_Ways_of_Thinking" class="extiw" title="s:Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking">Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking</a></i>, Lecture 2, fourth paragraph.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In addition to James's lectures and publications on pragmatist ideas (<i>Will to Believe</i> 1897, etc.) wherein he credited Peirce, James also arranged for two paid series of lectures by Peirce, including the 1903 Harvard lectures on pragmatism. See pp. 261–4, 290–2, &amp; 324 in Brent, Joseph (1998), <i>Charles Sanders Peirce: A Life</i>, 2nd edition.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-10">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, C. S., "The Founding of Pragmatism", manuscript written 1906, published in <i>The Hound &amp; Horn: A Harvard Miscellany</i> v. II, n. 3, April–June 1929, pp. 282–5, see 283–4, reprinted 1934 as "Historical Affinities and Genesis" in <i><a href="/wiki/Charles_Sanders_Peirce_bibliography#CP" title="Charles Sanders Peirce bibliography">Collected Papers</a></i> v. 5, paragraphs 11–13, see 12.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Shook, John (undated), "The Metaphysical Club", the <i>Pragmatism Cybrary</i>. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.pragmatism.org/research/metaphysical_club.htm">Eprint</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, C. S. (1877), <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/The_Fixation_of_Belief" class="extiw" title="s:The Fixation of Belief">The Fixation of Belief</a>, <i>Popular Science Monthly</i>, v. 12, pp. 1–15. Reprited often, including <i>Collected Papers</i> v. 5, paragraphs 358–87 and <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 1, pp. 109–23).</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-13">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, on p <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=j6oLAAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA165">p. 165</a>–166 in "What Pragmatism Is", <i>The Monist</i>, v. XV, n. 2, April 1905, pp. 161–81, reprinted in <i>Collected Papers</i> v. 5, paragraphs 411–37, see 414.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-14"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-14">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Manuscript "A Sketch of Logical Critics", <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 2, pp. 451–62, see pp. 457–8. Peirce wrote:</span>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p><span class="reference-text">I have always fathered my pragmati<i>ci</i>sm (as I have called it since James and Schiller made the word [<i>pragmatism</i>] imply "the will to believe," the mutability of truth, the soundness of Zeno's refutation of motion, and pluralism generally), upon Kant, Berkeley, and Leibniz....</span></p>
</blockquote>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-NA-15"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-NA_15-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-NA_15-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, C. S. (1908) "<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/A_Neglected_Argument_for_the_Reality_of_God" class="extiw" title="s:A Neglected Argument for the Reality of God">A Neglected Argument for the Reality of God</a>", <i>Hibbert Journal</i> 7, reprinted in <i>Collected Papers</i> v. 6, paragraphs 452–85, <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 2, 434–50, and elsewhere. After discussing James, Peirce stated (Section V, fourth paragraph) as the specific occasion of his coinage "pragmaticism", journalist, pragmatist, and literary author <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Papini" title="Giovanni Papini">Giovanni Papini</a>'s declaration of pragmatism's indefinability (see for example "What Is Pragmatism Like", a translation published in October 1907 in <i>Popular Science Monthly</i> v. 71, pp. 351–8, <i>Google Books</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=DKkWAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA351">Eprint</a>). Peirce in his closing paragraph wrote that "willing not to exert the will (willing to believe)" should not be confused with "active willing (willing to control thought, to doubt, and to weigh reasons)", and discussed his dismay by that which he called the other pragmatists' "angry hatred of strict logic". He also rejected their <a href="/wiki/Nominalism" title="Nominalism">nominalist</a> tendencies. But he remained allied with them about the falsity of necessitarianism and about the reality of generals and habits understood in terms of potential concrete effects even if unactualized.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-16"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-16">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, C. S. (1868) "Questions Concerning Certain Faculties Claimed For Man", <i>Journal of Speculative Philosophy</i> v. 2, n. 2, pp. 103–114. Reprinted <i>Collected Peirce</i> v. 5, paragraphs 213–263, <i>Writings</i> v. 2, pp. 193–211, <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 2, pp. 11–27, and elsewhere. <i>Peirce.org</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.peirce.org/writings/p26.html">Eprint</a>. <i>Google Books</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=YHkqP2JHJ_IC&amp;pg=RA1-PA140">Eprint</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-17"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-17">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Kasser, Jeff (1998), "Peirce's Supposed Psychologism" in <i>Transactions of the Charles S. Peirce Society</i>, v. 35, n. 3, summer 1999, pp. 501–527. <i>Arisbe</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cspeirce.com/menu/library/aboutcsp/kasser/psychol.htm">Eprint</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-18"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-18">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce held that (philosophical) logic is a <a href="/wiki/Normative" title="Normative">normative</a> field, that pragmatism is a method developed in it, and that philosophy, though not deductive or so general as mathematics, still concerns positive phenomena in general, including phenomena of matter and mind, without depending on special experiences or experiments such as those of <a href="/wiki/Optics" title="Optics">optics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Experimental_psychology" title="Experimental psychology">experimental psychology</a>, in both of which Peirce was active. See quotes under "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.helsinki.fi/science/commens/terms/philosophy.html">Philosophy</a>" at the <i>Commens Dictionary of Peirce's Terms</i>. Peirce also harshly criticized the Cartesian approach of starting from hyperbolic doubts rather than from the combination of established beliefs and genuine doubts. See the opening of his 1868 "Some Consequences of Four Incapacities", <i>Journal of Speculative Philosophy</i> v. 2, n. 3, pp. 140–157. Reprinted <i>Collected Papers</i> v. 5, paragraphs 264–317, <i>Writings</i> v. 2, pp. 211–42, and <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 1, pp. 28–55. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cspeirce.com/menu/library/bycsp/conseq/cn-frame.htm">Eprint</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-19"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-19">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce (1902), The Carnegie Institute Application, Memoir 10, MS L75.361-2, <i>Arisbe</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cspeirce.com/menu/library/bycsp/l75/ver1/l75v1-04.htm#m10">Eprint</a>.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-20"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-20">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Peirce, C. S. (1868), "Some Consequences of Four Incapacities", <i>Journal of Speculative Philosophy</i> v. 2, n. 3, p <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=YHkqP2JHJ_IC&amp;pg=RA1-PA140">p. 140</a>–57, see opening pages. Reprinted <i>Collected Papers</i> v. 5, paragraphs 264–317, <i>Writings</i> v. 2, pp. 211–42, <i>Essential Peirce</i> v. 1, pp. 28–55. <dt>Surveys</dt>
</dl>
<ul>
<li>John J. Stuhr, ed. <i>One Hundred Years of Pragmatism: William James's Revolutionary Philosophy</i> (Indiana University Press; 2010) 215 pages; Essays on pragmatism and American culture, pragmatism as a way of thinking and settling disputes, pragmatism as a theory of truth, and pragmatism as a mood, attitude, or temperament.</li>
</ul>
<p><b>Important introductory primary texts</b><br />
Note that this is an <i>introductory</i> list: some important works are left out and some less monumental works that are excellent introductions are included.</p>
<ul>
<li>C. S. Peirce, "<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/The_Fixation_of_Belief" class="extiw" title="s:The Fixation of Belief">The Fixation of Belief</a>" (paper)</li>
<li>C. S. Peirce, "<a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/How_to_Make_Our_Ideas_Clear" class="extiw" title="s:How to Make Our Ideas Clear">How to Make Our Ideas Clear</a>" (paper)</li>
<li>C. S. Peirce, "A Definition of Pragmatism" (paper as titled by Menand in <i>Pragmatism: A Reader</i>, from <i>Collected Papers of Charles Sanders Peirce</i> v. 8, some or all of paragraphs 191–195.)</li>
<li>William James, <i><a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Pragmatism:_A_New_Name_for_Some_Old_Ways_of_Thinking" class="extiw" title="s:Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking">Pragmatism: A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking</a></i> (especially lectures I, II and VI)</li>
<li>John Dewey, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=ZUg8AAAAIAAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover">Reconstruction in Philosophy</a></i></li>
<li>John Dewey, "Three Independent factors in Morals" (lecture published as paper)</li>
<li>John Dewey, "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://spartan.ac.brocku.ca/~lward/Dewey/Dewey_1910b/Dewey_1910_06.html">A short catechism concerning truth</a>" (chapter)</li>
<li>W. V. O. Quine, "Three Dogmas of Empiricism" (paper)</li>
</ul>

<li>Lorenzo Fabbri. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.academia.edu/998044/The_Domestication_of_Derrida_Rorty_Pragmatism_and_Deconstruction"><i>The domestication of Derrida: Rorty, pragmatism and deconstruction</i></a>. 2008</li>
<li>Richard Field. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.iep.utm.edu/d/dewey.htm#H5"><i>John Dewey (1859-1952)</i></a>. Internet Encyclopedia of Philosophy.</li>
<li>Peter H. Hare, Michel Weber, James K. Swindler, Oana-Maria Pastae, Cerasel Cuteanu (eds.), <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.academia.edu/280925/International_Perspectives_on_Pragmatism">International Perspectives on Pragmatism</a></i>, Newcastle upon Tyne, Cambridge Scholars Publishing, 2009 (<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9781443801942" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 978-1-4438-0194-2</a>).</li>
<li>David L. Hildebrand. <i>Beyond Realism &amp; Anti-Realism.</i> 2003.</li>
<li>David L. Hildebrand. <i>The Neopragmatist Turn.</i> Southwest Philosophy Review Vol. 19, no. 1. January, 2003.</li>
<li>William James. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gutenberg.org/etext/5116"><i>Pragmatism, A New Name for Some Old Ways of Thinking, Popular Lectures on Philosophy</i></a>. 1907.</li>
<li>William James <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://falcon.jmu.edu/~omearawm/ph101willtobelieve.html"><i>The Will to Believe</i></a>. 1896.</li>
<li>George Lakoff and Mark Johnson. <i>Philosophy in the Flesh&#160;: The Embodied Mind and Its Challenge to Western Thought.</i> 1999.</li>
<li>Todd Lekan. <i>Making Morality: Pragmatist Reconstruction in Ethical Theory.</i> 2003.</li>
<li>C.I. Lewis. <i>Mind and the World Order: Outline of a Theory of Knowledge.</i> 1929.</li>
<li>David Macarthur. “Pragmatism, Metaphysical Quietism and the Problem of Normativity,” Philosophical Topics Vol. 36 no.1, 2009.</li>
<li>Keya Maitra. <i>On Putnam.</i> 2003.</li>
<li>Joseph Margolis. <i>Historied Thought, Constructed World.</i> 1995.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Louis_Menand" title="Louis Menand">Louis Menand</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Metaphysical_Club:_A_Story_of_Ideas_in_America" title="The Metaphysical Club: A Story of Ideas in America">The Metaphysical Club</a>.</i> 2001.</li>
<li>Cheryl Misak (ed.) <i>The New Pragmatists.</i> Oxford University Press, 2007</li>
<li>Hilary Putnam <i>Reason, Truth and History.</i> 1981.</li>
<li>W.V.O. Quine. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ditext.com/quine/quine.html"><i>Two Dogmas of Empiricism</i></a>. Philosophical Review. January 1951.</li>
<li>W.V.O. Quine <i>Ontological Relativity and Other Essays.</i> 1969.</li>
<li>N. Rescher. <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://plato.stanford.edu/entries/process-philosophy/"><i>Process Philosophy</i></a>. The Stanford Encyclopedia of Philosophy.</li>
<li>Richard Rorty <i>Rorty Truth and Progress: Philosophical Papers. Volume 3.</i> 1998.</li>
<li>Stephen Toulmin. <i>The Uses of Argument.</i> 1958.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michel_Weber" title="Michel Weber">Michel Weber</a> (ed.), <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.academia.edu/279952/After_Whitehead_Rescher_on_Process_Metaphysics">After Whitehead: Rescher on Process Metaphysics</a></i>, Frankfurt / Paris / Lancaster, Ontos Verlag, 2004 (<a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/3937202498" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 3-937202-49-8</a>).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michel_Weber" title="Michel Weber">Michel Weber</a>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.academia.edu/392183/Whiteheads_Pancreativism._Jamesian_Applications">Whitehead's Pancreativism. Jamesian Applications</a></i>, Frankfurt / Paris, Ontos Verlag, 2011.</li>
<li>William Egginton/<a href="/wiki/Mike_Sandbothe" title="Mike Sandbothe">Mike Sandbothe</a> (Eds.) <i>The Pragmatic Turn in Philosophy. Contemporary Engagement between Analytic and Continental Thought.</i> 2004.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mike_Sandbothe" title="Mike Sandbothe">Mike Sandbothe</a>. <i>Pragmatic Media Philosophy.</i> 2005.</li>
